FOR EDUCATIONAL USE ONLY

Gian Singh v State Of Punjab & Another

Supreme Court of India

24 September 2012

Case Analysis

Bench

R.M. Lodha, A.R. Dave, Sudhansu Jyoti Mukhopadhaya

Where Reported

2012 Indlaw SC 314; (2012) 10 SCC 303; AIR 2012 SC (Supp) 838; 2012 CRLJ 4934; 2012 (5) CTC 526; JT 2012 (9) SC 426; 2012 (5) KarLJ 476; 2012 (4) KLT 108; 2012 (4) Law Herald (P&H) 3025; 2012 (4) RCR(Criminal) 543; 2013 (4) RLW 3573; 2012(9) SCALE 257; [2012] 8 S.C.R. 753; 2012 (4) WLN(SC) 71

Case Digest

Subject: Criminal; Practice & Procedure

Keywords: Prevention of Corruption Act

Summary: Criminal - Practice & Procedure - Indian Penal Code, 1860, ss. 120-B, 420 - Code of Criminal Procedure, 1973, ss. 320, 320(7) and 482 - Criminal conspiracy - Compoundable - Permissibility - Appellant (accused) was convicted for offences u/ss. 120-B and 420 of IPC by Trial Court - Aggrieved appellant filed appeal before Lower Appellate Court, and filed an application for compounding the offences - However, appellant filed a petition u/s. 482 of CrPC before HC to quash FIR - HC dismissed the petition - Aggrieved appellant filed appeals before SC relying on SC decisions in B.S.Joshi and others v. State of Haryana and another, 2003 Indlaw SC 230, Nikhil Merchant v. Central Bureau of Investigation and another, 2008 Indlaw SC 1321 and Manoj Sharma v. State and others, 2008 Indlaw SC 2064, wherein SC had indirectly permitted compounding of non-compoundable offences - However, SC did not permit offence u/s. 120-B of IPC to be compounded and held that non-compoundable offences could not compounded by Court whether directly or indirectly - SC doubted the correctness of relied judgments - Hence, instant reference to larger bench - Whether non-compoundable offence could be compounded by the HCs - Held, s. 482 of CrPC, saved inherent power of HC which it had by virtue of it being a superior Court to prevent abuse of process of any Court or otherwise to secure the ends of justice - Words, 'nothing in this Code' (CrPC) left no manner of doubt that none of the provisions of CrPC limited or restricted the inherent power - Power u/s. 482 of CrPC merely safeguarded existing inherent powers possessed by HC necessary to prevent abuse of process of any Court or to secure ends of justice - Such power should be exercised very sparingly and it should not be exercised as against the express bar of law engrafted in any other provision of CrPC - Power possessed by HC u/s. 482 of CrPC was of wide amplitude but required exercise with great caution and circumspection - It was neither permissible nor proper for Court to provide a straitjacket formula regulating the exercise of inherent powers u/s.482 of CrPC - No precise and inflexible guidelines could be provided - Power of compounding of offences given to a Court u/s. 320 of CrPC was materially different from quashing of criminal proceedings by HC in exercise of its inherent jurisdiction - In compounding of offences, formation of opinion by HC for quashing a criminal offence or criminal proceeding or criminal complaint was guided by material on record as to whether the ends of justice would justify - HC quashed a criminal proceeding having regard to fact that dispute between offender and victim was settled although offences were not compoundable, it did so as in its opinion, continuation of criminal proceedings would be an exercise in futility and justice in the case demands that dispute between parties was put to an end and peace was restored; securing the ends of justice was the ultimate guiding factor - HC might within the framework of its inherent power, quashed criminal proceeding or criminal complaint or FIR if it was satisfied that on the face of such settlement, there was hardly any likelihood of offender being convicted and by not quashing the criminal proceedings, justice should be casualty and ends of justice would be defeated - Each case would depend on its own facts and no hard and fast category could be prescribed - Judgments in cases of B.S.Joshi, Nikhil Merchant and Manoj Sharma did illustrate the principle that HC might quash criminal proceedings or FIR or complaint in exercise of its inherent power u/s. 482 of CrPC and s. 320 of CrPC did not limit or affect the powers of HC u/s. 482 of CrPC - By quashing criminal proceedings in B.S.Joshi, Nikhil Merchant and Manoj Sharma, SC did not compound the non-compoundable offences indirectly - There did exist the distinction between compounding of an offence u/s. 320 of CrPC and quashing of a criminal case by HC in exercise of inherent power u/s. 482 of CrPC - Two powers were distinct and different although ultimate consequence might be same viz., acquittal of accused or dismissal of indictment - Inherent power was of wide plentitude with no statutory limitation but had to exercise in accord with guidelines engrafted in such power viz., to secure the ends of justice or to prevent abuse of process of any Court - HC should have due regard to the nature and gravity of crime - Offences of mental depravity or offences like murder, rape, dacoity, etc., could not be fittingly quashed even though the victim or victim's family and offender had settled the dispute - Such offences were not private in nature and had serious impact on society - Any compromise between victim and offender in offences related under special statutes like Prevention of Corruption Act or offences committed by public servants while working in that capacity etc; could not provide for any basis for quashing criminal proceedings involving such offences - Thus, it could not be said that cases in B.S.Joshi, Nikhil Merchant and Manoj Sharma were not correctly decided - Reference answered.
